##### 13#       发表于 2023-2-13 11:11

比起新闻我更喜欢看评论，鬼鬼</blockquote>
美国民众在网上说，这就是美国的切尔诺贝利，政府正在不断“击落飞行物”，分散美国人的注意力。列车出轨事故时决定就地点燃车厢和“受控燃烧”也许有一定的道理，但是告诉居民“目前水和空气是安全”的，并告诉所有人“一切都很好”，这操作就太操蛋了。这可是美国本土，肥沃的农业州俄亥俄。前几个月，联邦政府强制解散了美国铁路总工会，并且强制让**抗议的铁路工人工作，很多人认为火车出轨是因为工人没得到休息疲劳驾驶，并且没了工会，连必要的检修都不做了；这次有个调查记者冒死去采样，然后就被当地警察逮捕了。泄露是难以避免的事故，但逮捕记者和新闻压制就是系统性的病态社会了。像极了一部美国电影《尸骨无存》，发生这么大的事情居然都没上推特和脸书热搜，美国掩盖舆论真有一手。

工作人员当天发现5节装载压缩氯乙烯的车厢释压装置停止工作，其中一节车厢内出现“急剧温度变化”，有潜在爆炸风险。为避免“灾难性”后果，诺福克南方公司6日决定在专家和应急人员协助下对上述5节车厢进行“受控释放”，把氯乙烯排入一个事先准备好的坑道内引爆并使其持续燃烧，避免这种有毒气体扩散到空中。<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/003.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

####  Karajan  
##### 136#       发表于 2023-2-13 16:03

<blockquote><strong>Times Beach, Missouri</strong>[size=0.875em]4 languages
[size=0.8125em][Article](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri)[Talk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talk:Times_Beach,_Missouri)

[Read](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri)[Edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit)[View history](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=history)

From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

Times Beach
Ghost town
<[img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/USA_Missouri_location_map.svg/250px-USA_Missouri_location_map.svg.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">
Times Beach

Location in Missouri

Show map of MissouriShow map of the United StatesShow all
Coordinates: <img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/WMA_button2b.png/17px-WMA_button2b.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">CountryUnited StatesStateMissouriCountySt. Louis CountyFounded1925Dis-incorporated1985Elevation
436 ft (133 m)<strong>Times Beach</strong> is a [ghost town](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghost_town) in [St. Louis County](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis_County,_Missouri), [Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missouri), United States, 17 miles (27 km) southwest of [St. Louis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri) and 2 miles (3 km) east of [Eureka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eureka,_Missouri). Once home to more than two thousand people, the town was completely evacuated early in 1983 due to [TCDD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2,3,7,8-Tetrachlorodibenzodioxin)—also known as [dioxin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dioxins_and_dioxin-like_compounds)—contamination. It was the largest civilian exposure to the compound in the history of the United States.In 1985, the State of Missouri officially disincorporated the city of Times Beach. The site of Times Beach now houses a 419-acre (170 ha) [state park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_66_State_Park) commemorating [U.S. Route 66](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Route_66)—the famous highway that stretched from [Chicago, Illinois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois), to [Santa Monica, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California), and passed by the community on its southern end—as well as the history of the Times Beach area.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Remember-1) The park opened in 1999.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Encyc-2) In 2001, the EPA removed Times Beach from its [Superfund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superfund) list.[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-3)<strong>History[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1)]</strong>Times Beach was founded in 1925 on the [flood plain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flood_plain) of the [Meramec River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meramec_River), southwest of the river, in a promotion by the now-defunct [St. Louis Star-Times](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis_Star-Times) newspaper. A purchase of a 20 × 100 ft (6 by 30 m) lot for $67.50 included a six-month newspaper subscription.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Remember-1)[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-SR-4)In its early years, the town was primarily a summer [resort](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resort_town), but the [Great Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression) combined with gasoline [rationing during World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rationing_in_the_United_States) reduced the feasibility of [summer homes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Summer_home).[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-SR-4) The town became a community of mostly [low-income housing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low-income_housing), and a small population (1,240) lived in Times Beach by 1970.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-SR-4) In the years immediately before its evacuation, Times Beach had become a lower-middle-class town.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-SR-4) Historically, there had always been a small grocery store and gas station on Route 66 to serve the residents.[[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed)]Prone to flooding throughout its history—its first buildings were built on stilts[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-SR-4)—the town experienced a devastating flood in December 1982. It happened just as the [Environmental Protection Agency (EPA)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency) was confirming that dioxin contaminated the soil,[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-5) leading to the town's evacuation by 1985[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Encyc-2) and complete demolition by 1992.[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-6) The town was disincorporated by executive order of [Missouri governor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Missouri) [John Ashcroft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Ashcroft) on April 2, 1985.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-7)The story of Times Beach was featured on [History Channel's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_(U.S._TV_channel)) [Modern Marvels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Marvels), in the episode "Engineering Disasters 20".[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-8)<strong>Dioxin contamination[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2)]</strong><strong>Events leading up to the crisis[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3)]</strong><strong>NEPACCO chemical waste disposal[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4)]</strong>During the late 1960s, the [Northeastern Pharmaceutical and Chemical Company, Inc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NEPACCO). (NEPACCO) began operating out of a facility located near [Verona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verona,_Missouri), in southwestern Missouri. This facility was owned by Hoffman-Taff, a company that produced the [Agent Orange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agent_Orange) herbicide for use during the [Vietnam War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam_War).[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9) By the time NEPACCO ceased its operations in 1972, Hoffman-Taff had been taken over by Syntex Agribusiness.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hites-10)From 1970 to 1972, NEPACCO was primarily involved in the production of [hexachlorophene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hexachlorophene) <strong>(3)</strong>, an antibacterial agent used in soap, toothpaste, and common household disinfectants, from 2,4,5-trichlorophenol <strong>(1)</strong> and formaldehyde <strong>(2)</strong>.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9)[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hites-10)<[img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Hexachlorophenesynthesis.png/400px-Hexachlorophenesynthesis.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

2,4,5-trichlorophenol is synthesized from 1,2,4,5-tetrachlorobenzene by the [nucleophilic aromatic substitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleophilic_aromatic_substitution) reaction with sodium hydroxide (NaOH). Unfortunately, instantaneous [dimerization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dimer_(chemistry)) of the resulting [phenol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenol) produces trace amounts of [2,3,7,8-tetrachlorodibenzo-p-dioxin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2,3,7,8-tetrachlorodibenzo-p-dioxin) (TCDD), an extremely toxic compound known to have both acute and chronic adverse effects.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hites-10)<[img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Seveso_reaction_de.svg/400px-Seveso_reaction_de.svg.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

Beginning the process of production with 2,4,5-trichlorophenol that contained 3–5 parts per million (ppm) of dioxin, NEPACCO was able to reduce the concentration of dioxin in hexachlorophene to 0.1 ppm.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11) The result of this purification process led to the storage and accumulation of heavily concentrated dioxin still bottoms, or thick, oily residues, in a storage tank located near the facility in Verona. When NEPACCO first began operations, the still bottoms were sent to a waste facility in Louisiana for incineration.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9) Although incineration was the best method to destroy dioxins at the time, it was also very expensive. Looking for less costly alternatives, NEPACCO contracted the services of the Independent Petrochemical Corporation (IPC).[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11) However, IPC, a chemical supplier company, knew very little about waste disposal, and subcontracted the NEPACCO job to Russell Martin Bliss, the owner of a small, local waste oil business. Charging NEPACCO $3000 per load, IPC paid Bliss $125 per load.Between February and October 1971, Bliss collected six truckloads (nearly 18,500 gallons) of chemical waste heavily contaminated with dioxin. Bliss took most of the still bottoms to his storage facility near [Frontenac, Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frontenac,_Missouri), where the contaminated NEPACCO waste was unloaded and mixed into tanks containing used motor oils. Subsequently, some of the contaminated oil was sold to MT Richards, a fuel company in Illinois, and to the Midwest Oil Refining Company in [Overland, Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overland,_Missouri).[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9)<strong>First cases of contamination[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5)]</strong>In addition to his waste oil business, Bliss owned a horse arena and farm, where he sprayed waste oils to control the problem of dust. One application kept the dust down for several months. Those who visited Bliss' property were impressed by how well the technique worked. It was not long before people began to hire him for his dust-suppressant services.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)On May 26, 1971, the owners of Shenandoah Stable, located near [Moscow Mills, Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moscow_Mills,_Missouri), Judy Piatt and Frank Hampel, paid Bliss $150 to spray the floor of their indoor arena.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9)[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Sun-12) The waste oil sprayed, which totaled a volume of 2,000 gallons, was uncharacteristically thick, and left a pungent, burning odor.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Allen-13) Within a few days of the spraying, birds began to drop dead from the rafters of the barns, and horses began to develop sores and lose their hair. Piatt and Hampel blamed these occurrences on Bliss, who denied responsibility, claiming that the material he sprayed was nothing more than old motor oil.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9)Acting on their suspicions, Piatt and Hampel removed the top six inches of soil from the entire arena and disposed of it in a landfill. Despite the removal of another 12 inches of soil a few months later, the horses that came to the arena still became ill.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11) After several months, 62 horses died or became so emaciated that they had to be euthanized. Hampel, Piatt, and Piatt's two young daughters also became ill, developing headaches, nosebleeds, abdominal pain, and diarrhea.[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Allen-13)A month after the spraying at Shenandoah, Bliss was hired to spray the arena at Timberline Stables, near [Jefferson City, Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jefferson_City,_Missouri). Twelve horses died, and children exposed to the arena were diagnosed with [chloracne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chloracne), a skin condition associated with [dioxin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dioxin) poisoning.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Suskind-14) Suspecting that Bliss' oil was the source of their problems, the owners of Timberline removed the top layer of soil from their property.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)A third arena, at Bubbling Springs Ranch, near St. Louis, was also sprayed around the same time as Timberline and faced similar problems. As at Shenandoah and Timberline, the owners decided to remove the top layer of soil from their arena. Vernon Stout, a road-grading contractor, completed the removal in March 1973. Instead of bringing the soil to a landfill, however, Stout unloaded the soil onto one of his properties and at the nearby home of Harold Minker.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)<strong>CDC investigations[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6)]</strong>The unexplained deaths and illnesses at Shenandoah immediately caught the attention of the [Centers for Disease Control and Prevention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention) (CDC). In August 1971, the CDC completed an inspection of Shenandoah Stable, and collected human and animal blood samples, as well as soil samples.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9) Although initial results revealed that the soil at Shenandoah Stable contained PCBs and chlorinated insecticides, the CDC was unable to identify a specific chemical culprit. It was not until 1973 that tests revealed the presence of [trichlorophenol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trichlorophenol).[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Allen-13) When trace amounts of the crude trichlorophenol contaminant were administered to the inner surfaces of rabbit ears, blisters developed, which was a characteristic result of trichlorophenol poisoning.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9) The unexpected death of some of the affected rabbits however, led the CDC to run more complex tests.On July 30, 1974, the CDC found that, in addition to 5,000 ppm of trichlorophenol and 1,590 ppm of [PCBs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polychlorinated_biphenyl), the soil samples collected from Shenandoah contained over 30 ppm of dioxin.[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Allen-13) Although little was known about the effects of dioxin on humans, the lethality of small doses in animals was alarming. As a result, the CDC immediately set out to locate other possible sites of contamination. When confronted by the CDC, Bliss stated that he did not know where the dioxin could have come from.Because dioxin was a by-product of only a handful of chemicals, trichlorophenol being the most common, the CDC narrowed their search to companies in Missouri using or producing trichlorophenol. NEPACCO was the only company on the search list that had come into contact with Bliss.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)NEPACCO went out of business in 1972, after the [Food and Drug Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Food_and_Drug_Administration) (FDA) had issued a ban that limited the use of hexachlorophene. The ban was motivated by the death of thirty-two infants in France who were exposed to high levels of hexachlorophene in baby powder.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9) During an inspection of the old NEPACCO facility in Verona, which was now entirely owned by Syntex Agribusiness, the CDC discovered an old tank filled with 4,300 gallons of NEPACCO still bottoms at a dioxin concentration of more than 340 ppm. Due to a lack of incinerators in proximity to the Verona plant, the proper disposal of the leftover still bottoms would not be completed until 1979.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)With further investigation of contaminated locations, the CDC advised residents of the Minker and Stout properties to minimize contact with the soil. Soil samples had revealed a dioxin concentration of 0.85 ppm at Minker's property, and a concentration of 0.44 ppm at Stout's property. In a 1975 confidential report to the [Environmental Protection Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Agency) (EPA), the CDC also further advised the removal and burial of contaminated soil from both properties. In the same document, however, the CDC reported that the [half-life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Half-life) of dioxin was one year.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15) Based on this estimate, which was later found to be incorrect, Missouri officials decided to forgo the recommended cleanup.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11) Today, the half-life of dioxin is estimated to be seven to eleven years.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-16)<strong>Involvement of the EPA[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7)]</strong>The EPA did not become heavily involved with the Missouri dioxin contaminations until 1979 when a former NEPACCO employee reported the burial of toxic waste on a farm located about seven miles from Verona. NEPACCO had paid James Denney, the owner of the farm, $150 for the use of his property. Under the investigations of the EPA, a total of 90 drums, all of which were corroded and leaky, were unearthed. Eleven of these drums contained still bottoms with dioxin concentrations as high as 2,000 ppm.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15)In May and June 1982, the EPA decided to revisit the Shenandoah, Timberline, and Bubbling Springs stables, as well as the Minker and Stout properties. New soil samples revealed that concentrations of dioxin had not decreased since the last test results obtained by the CDC several years earlier. Although eleven years had passed since the spraying, areas in the Shenandoah arena still contained as much as 1.8 ppm of dioxin. Regional EPA officials advised owners of the contaminated stables to temporarily close and urged the national EPA office to begin cleanup operations at each of the contaminated locations. These cleanup requests were delayed when [Rita Lavelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rita_Lavelle), an assistant administrator at EPA headquarters in Washington, announced that the EPA would be collecting and testing an additional 600 soil samples in order to better understand the extent of contamination.[[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed)]The EPA's handling of the events in Missouri caught national attention in late 1982 when the [Environmental Defense Fund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_Defense_Fund), a public interest group, published a leaked EPA document that listed a total of 14 confirmed and 41 possibly contaminated sites in the state of Missouri. The town of Times Beach was one of the locations listed. The Environmental Defense Fund also claimed that the EPA had decided to lower dioxin cleanup protocol standards. Although the CDC advised for cleanups in locations where dioxin levels were as low as 0.001 ppm, the Environmental Defense Fund report suggested that new EPA protocols would only necessitate clean up in locations where dioxin concentrations were above 0.1 ppm.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9)<strong>Crisis at Times Beach[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8)]</strong><strong>Double disaster[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9)]</strong>In 1972, Times Beach hired Bliss to oil its 23 miles of dirt roads (due to lack of funding, Times Beach was unable to pave its roads). For $2,400, Bliss sprayed approximately 160,000 gallons of waste oil in Times Beach over a period of four years.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15) The release of the leaked EPA document in 1982 was the first time that Times Beach had learned of its contamination.[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Allen-13) Residents felt betrayed and publicly criticized the EPA for not informing them of the toxic hazards around their homes.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15) Since Times Beach had the largest population out of the listed sites, Times Beach became the subject of national media and attention.[[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed)]With pressure from the public, the EPA soon began investigation in Times Beach. Soil sampling was fortuitously completed on December 3, 1982, a day before Times Beach suffered its worst flood in history when the [Meramec River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meramec_River) breached its banks and rose over 14 feet above [flood stage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flood_stage).[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Sun-12)[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15) The residents of Times Beach were evacuated, and by the time the waters began to recede, the EPA had concluded its analysis. Results revealed dioxin concentrations as high as 0.3 ppm along the town's entire network of roads.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)<strong>Buyout and cleanup efforts[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10)]</strong>On December 23, 1982, the CDC publicly recommended that Times Beach not be re-inhabited. Officials were uncertain about the health effects of extensive dioxin exposure and even more uncertain of how to rid an entire town of dioxin. Because the town was situated on a flood plain, officials were further concerned that subsequent flooding would spread the contamination beyond control.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9)Discussions of a federal buyout commenced on January 7, 1983, when President [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan) created the Times Beach Dioxin Task Force, which consisted of representatives from the EPA, CDC, [Federal Emergency Management Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency) (FEMA), and [Army Corps of Engineers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army_Corps_of_Engineers). During a press conference on February 22, 1983, the EPA announced that the federal government would pay $33.0 million of the estimated $36.7 million cost to buy out the 800 residential properties and 30 businesses of Times Beach. The remaining $3.7 million would be the responsibility of the state.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15)By 1985, Times Beach's entire population of well over 2,000 residents had been relocated, and [Governor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_Missouri) [John Ashcroft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Ashcroft) had issued an executive order for the town's dis-incorporation.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-17)Since it contained over 50 percent of the dioxin in the state of Missouri and because it was no longer inhabited, Times Beach was the logical choice for the placement of a new incinerator. The construction of the incinerator began in June 1995. Once built, it burned more than 265,000 tons of dioxin-contaminated materials from across the state. The cleanup of Missouri was completed in 1997 and had cost close to $200 million.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9)[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Allen-13)<strong>Legal action and responsibility[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11)]</strong>In response to the events that transpired in Missouri during the 1970s, a number of laws were passed to regulate the generation and disposal of potentially hazardous products. In 1976, Congress passed the [Toxic Substances Control Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toxic_Substances_Control_Act), which required the testing of chemicals that could pose an unreasonable risk to the environment. In 1976, Congress also passed the [Resource Conservation and Recovery Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resource_Conservation_and_Recovery_Act) (RCRA), which regulated the transportation and disposal of hazardous waste.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15) In 1980, the passage of the [Comprehensive Environmental Response, Compensation, and Liability Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comprehensive_Environmental_Response,_Compensation,_and_Liability_Act) (CERCLA) established a multibillion-dollar [Superfund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superfund) to investigate and clean up old, abandoned hazardous waste sites.The passage of CERCLA also defined the liability of a company and ensured that parties responsible for the release of toxic substances are held liable in the case of environmental damage or harm. In 1983, the federal government sued NEPACCO and its officers, Edwin Michaels and John W. Lee, in United States v. Northeastern Pharmaceutical and Chemical Co.. Under the provisions of CERCLA, NEPACCO was forced to repay the federal government for its cleanup efforts at the farm of James Denney, the site where NEPACCO had buried ninety drums of its chemical waste over a decade earlier.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11)[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-18)[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-19)[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-20)Because the RCRA was not implemented until 1976, Bliss was not legally required to keep records of the chemical wastes he had collected from NEPACCO. During investigations surrounding the dioxin contamination in Missouri, Bliss maintained that he had no knowledge of the presence of dioxin in the chemical waste he collected from NEPACCO.[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Sun-12) Still, Bliss was the object of many legal pursuits. Over 14,000 citizens' suits were filed against NEPACCO and its officers, Syntex Agribusiness, IPC, and Bliss.[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Gough-11) Among these were the cases of Piatt and Hample, who in 1976 settled their suit against Bliss for $10,000 and against IPC for $100,000. In 1981, Piatt and Hample also settled for $65,000 from NEPACCO. IPC paid $1 million to each of Piatt's daughters in 1983.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15)<strong>Consequences of the contamination[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12)]</strong>Although the decision for relocation in 1982 was made in the best interests and safety of the Times Beach residents, the evacuation was not an easy transition. Eight hundred families had to leave their lives completely behind. Initially, parents worried about what to do and where to go for financial assistance. As they began to settle into their new lives, their logistical and financial worries were soon replaced by the fear that their children would be afflicted by sudden chronic illnesses. The psychological trauma caused by relocation was immeasurable.[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Hernan-9)<[img src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Route_66_Times_Beach_visitor_center.jpg/220px-Route_66_Times_Beach_visitor_center.jpg" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">[size=12.3704px]

The former roadhouse, now the Route 66 State Park Visitor Center in January 2017
</blockquote>

The land that was once Times Beach is now [Route 66 State Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_66_State_Park). One building from the town still exists: the park's visitor center was once a roadhouse from Times Beach's glory days and was the EPA's headquarters for the area. There is a large grass mound beneath which is the debris of the demolished buildings of the former town.[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-hernan-21) The EPA revisited and tested the soil at the Route 66 State Park in June 2012. On November 19, 2012, it was reported that "Soil samples from Route 66 State Park show no significant health risks for park visitors or workers."[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-22)<strong>Controversy[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Times_Beach,_Missouri&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13)]</strong>Several months after the evacuation, the [American Medical Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Medical_Association) (AMA) publicly criticized the news media for spreading unscientific information about dioxin and the health hazards associated with it. The AMA stated that there was no evidence of adverse consequences from low-level dioxin exposure. Subsequent studies of potentially exposed people from Times Beach and some other contaminated locations in Missouri have revealed no adverse health outcomes that can be directly linked to dioxin.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Wildavsky-15) In a study conducted by the CDC and the Missouri Division of Health, no cases of [chloracne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chloracne), a common symptom of acute dioxin poisoning, were observed in Times Beach residents.[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-Suskind-14)By May 1991, Dr Vernon Houk, the director of the CDC's Center for Environmental Health, had come to the same conclusion as the AMA. Although he had made the official recommendation to permanently relocate Times Beach residents in 1982, by 1991, he no longer believed that evacuation had been necessary.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Times_Beach,_Missouri#cite_note-23)[[better source needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS)]
维基上关于时代海滩事件的记录，当初是拿有机废料撒在土地上抑尘，其中一个马厩撒了2000加仑，从马厩土壤取样，5000ppm的三氯苯酚，1590ppm的多氯联苯，30ppm的二噁英，农场的鸟都死了，几个月死了60多匹马，农场主出现了一系列的病症。
关键是后面AMA跳反，说这些问题和二噁英的联系并不确定，所以咯，让美国人当小白鼠呗，我们看戏好了。

####  xjjgp01

<blockquote>劲霸男 发表于 2023-2-13 17:27
氢弹还能改变物质成分吗？二噁英炸一遍还是二噁英吧？</blockquote>
分子化学性质稳定是因为在当前条件下没有足够能量促使它产生变化，一般城市垃圾不完全燃烧（300-400℃）容易产生二噁英，但有一种清洁的垃圾焚烧方法就是利用做陶瓷的高炉焚烧，内部3000℃以上的高温，即使燃烧过程中有少量二噁英产生也能迅速被高温分解为无污染的小分子，所以我赞成往美国多投几颗大伊万什么的<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/032.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

选票是生命，媒体是影响民意选票的最重要工具，故而成熟的选票民主必然发展出强大的媒体操控能力，这才是正常的逻辑。

这个国家热衷于在海外推广选票民主，也是因为他们有成熟的对媒体的方法论，以及现成的影响力，可以方便的通过该国媒体为杠杆插手影响该国的政局，成本低，效果好。

什么新闻自由是基石？这恰恰就证明了他们强大的宣传力，才让你相信了这种鬼话

####  9号单开道岔  
##### 265#       发表于 2023-2-13 22:15

<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59732118&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">poor 发表于 2023-2-13 20:38</a>

所以高合法性神国啥意思？我百度过了还不知道</blockquote>
瞎猜是这个意思，美国自称“山巅之城”

1629年夏季，马萨诸塞公司派遣六艘船，搭载了300多名移民前往新英格兰。1630年春天，英国乡绅约翰·温斯罗普(John Winthrop)以"阿贝拉号"为旗舰，率领十六、七艘船只(1000多名移民，而且多数是家庭)出英格兰，前往其"应许之地"新英格兰。他把这次海上之旅与摩西率领犹太民众出埃及相提并论。在旅途中，他为船上的旅伴做了如下"山巅之城"(参《马太福音》5:14-16)的着名布道，为美国历史奠定了恒久的基调，成为此后学界广泛讨论的"美国例外论"(American Exceptionalism)的滥觞。

"山巅之城"一词出自《马太福音》第五章第14节:"你们是世上的光，城造在山上是不能隐藏的"。清教徒相信上帝与他们有个契约，并挑选他们领导地球上的其余国家。约翰·温斯罗普充满希望地将马萨诸塞湾的宗教领地描绘成"山巅之城"。

####  ccchirose  
##### 273#       发表于 2023-2-13 22:54

 本帖最后由 ccchirose 于 2023-2-13 22:55 编辑 
<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59732118&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">poor 发表于 2023-2-13 20:38</a>

所以高合法性神国啥意思？我百度过了还不知道</blockquote>
高合法性，是指美帝的外在表现，具有强大的舆论场域，无论国内还是国外的负面事件，都有非常好的基础稳定性，很难动摇政府的统治力、削弱美帝人民对共同体的想象力、有损于世界人民对其的形象认知。

神国，是指美帝的内部核心，高合法性相当程度上来自于先验的、非理性的、不言自明的上帝选民神话，建构于山巅之城世所唯一的国家叙事，远远超过其现世应当有的国家实力和治理表现。

现实中政府要取信于你，需要大量的事实来佐证，还得看过往表现构成的信用记录；但神国不需要，因为神不可以质疑和讨论，不能用理性来理解推敲。

*****

####  Mr.Cheung  
##### 291#       发表于 2023-2-13 23:54

 本帖最后由 Mr.Cheung 于 2023-2-14 00:00 编辑 
<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59734124&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">RookieTnT 发表于 2023-2-13 23:19</a>

2017年，诺福克南方铁路通过游说，使得为运输危险品的列车配备电空制动系统的规定被废除。所以知道 ...</blockquote>
<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/005.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

其实还真没有这么简单

<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/034.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

在这件事情上，国内群众包括泥潭大部分人吃瓜的心态确实还是受到了自身所处环境的局限性影响，多少有点想当然，所以觉得特别劲爆特别离谱

但是如果你知道过去五六年之间美国的铁路货运系统发生了什么变化以及其现状的话就知道出这种事情一点都不令人意外，甚至可以说几乎就是个必然，迟早而已

和长期没什么存在感，被提起也大多是嘲笑的客运业务不同，美国的铁路货运实际上经营状况近年来实际上是相当不错的，利润蒸蒸日上，但与此同时事故率也是逐年攀升，这两者实际上都是一件事造成的两种后果，亦即美国七大一级铁路货运公司（所谓Class one公司，七大公司加起来营收占全行业的90%以上）的经营理念的转变带来的。

在过去十年间，这些公司全都采用了所谓的“精确时刻规划铁路运营法”（Precision Scheduled Railroading）的经营理念，简称PSR，这玩意儿你可以说本意上是要让铁路经营更灵活反应更快提升效率，但实践中其实就是从以往的“货等车”变成“车等货”，就是说以前是每天开固定班次的车，你货运来了赶不上就只能等下一趟车，现在就改成了每天开车班次不固定，货到了车装满了就可以出发，更灵活，但代价就是让车组人员过上了极为反人类的生活

<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/009.gif" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

简单来说，如果你是七大货运公司的货运列车车组人员，他们叫conductor和engineer（可以理解为火车司机和随车工程师，每次货运列车出车都各需要一位），那你就需要长时间处于24小时待命的状态<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/226.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">从接到电话开始的平均到岗时间要求是90分钟。

<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/020.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

等你放下手头的事情赶到公司指定车站出车，就开始干活吧，连续12小时不带停的，然后因为联邦法律规定的工作时长到了，你可以停下，前往公司在附近为你准备好的旅馆获得10小时休息时间，这10小时内不会有电话来，你爱干嘛干嘛，10小时一过，恢复待命状态，周而复始<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/152.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/005.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

这样的生活就导致了这些开货运列车的conductor和engineer处于长期的焦虑紧张状态，作息不规律，也很难得到良好的休息，更没有时间处理个人和家庭事务（理论上会有休假额度，但需要提前两个月申请，然后公司看情况决定批不批准），近两年更是把以往的可以临时紧急请假的Mark off制度取消了改用积分制，除非提前两个月申请，否则凡是请假就要扣分，病假也不例外<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/037.png" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">

####  天网  
##### 293#       发表于 2023-2-14 00:06

 本帖最后由 天网 于 2023-2-14 00:07 编辑 
<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59734372&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">FanFun 发表于 2023-2-13 23:39</a>

以前有个词叫洗 脑，还特别喜欢在游戏里设置为红色阵营的能力，现在看还是西方阵营的对民众洗 脑能力逆天 ...</blockquote>
这个事其实深究很有意思。英辞典对洗脳的词源考就是朝鲜战争期间通过中文逆输出出去的（[brainwashing](https://www.etymonline.com/word/brainwashing)：1950, said to be a literal translation of Chinese xi nao. A term from the Korean War ）。最早使用这个词是因为不理解为什么美国战俘经常被轻易的说服然后就被投了

尤里的设定起源也和这个类似，原型是列宁（westwood制作人员承认过），他演讲很有煽动力，而且能通过第三国际大量输出革命搅得全球一片红，看起来就像掌握了精神控制的技术一样。

理解不了康米的感召力，就用这种词汇来解释，就像用弱智的黑豹电影来庸俗化和解构黑豹精神一样。

不过这些事也早就俱往矣了，现在东大作为996和企业是爹的资本主义的最后堡垒可能自己人都没多少信的。确实是轮到西方文化胜利，看起来就像精神控制一样了

####  Dgnic_  
##### 312#       发表于 2023-2-14 01:29

随意来几篇外媒的报道：

Officials from the National Transportation Safety Board (NTSB) said there were 20 rail cars carrying hazardous material on the train. Ten of them derailed about 15 miles south of Youngstown, Ohio.
美国国家运输安全委员会（NTSB）的官员说，火车上有 20 节载有危险物品的火车车厢。其中 10 辆在俄亥俄州扬斯敦以南约 15 英里处脱轨。
Five of the derailed cars were carrying the chemical vinyl chloride, a type of gas.
其中五节脱轨的车厢载有化学物质氯乙烯，一种气体。
Exposure to vinyl chloride has been associated with heightened risks of certain forms of cancer, according to the National Cancer Institute - but state environmental officials said harmful levels had not been detected in the community.
根据美国国家癌症研究所的数据，接触氯乙烯与某些癌症的风险增加有关，但州环境官员表示，在社区中尚未检测到有害水平。

Despite assurances from Norfolk Southern, The Washington Postreported that "residents returning to homes in a neighboring Pennsylvania town were advised by state officials to open their windows, turn on fans, and wipe down all surfaces with diluted bleach."
《华盛顿 邮报》报道称，尽管诺福克南方做出了保证，但 “宾夕法尼亚州官员建议返回邻近城镇的居民打开窗户，打开风扇，并用稀释的漂白剂擦拭所有表面。“
One resident told the Post that her family experienced headaches and nausea in the wake of the derailment. She expressed concern that local officials are suppressing information about the health consequences of the crash and release of chemicals, which sent an alarming plume of dark smoke into the air.
一位居民告诉邮报，她的家人在脱轨后出现了头痛和恶心。她对当地官员压制有关坠机和化学物质释放对健康造成的后果的信息表示担忧，这些化学物质向空气中排放了令人担忧的黑烟。

In the 10 days after the derailment, observers have lamented the lack of media attention the situation in East Palestine has garnered relative to other recent stories, including the U.S. military's downing of several unidentified objects over the past week.
在脱轨事件发生后的 10 天里，观察人士哀叹，与最近的其他报道相比，东巴勒斯坦局势缺乏媒体的关注，包括美军在过去一周击落了几个不明物体。
Nina Turner, a former Ohio state senator, argued that "one of the reasons the media is so silent about the Norfolk Southern disaster in East Palestine, OH is due in part to classism."
前俄亥俄州州参议员尼娜・特纳认为，“媒体对东巴勒斯坦诺福克南部灾难保持沉默的原因之一，部分是由于阶级歧视。“
"If there were toxic chemicals being released in a wealthy suburban area, there would be outrage," Turner wrote on Twitter. "The silence is inexcusable."
特纳在推特上写道：“如果有有毒化学物质在富裕的郊区被释放，会引起愤怒。”“沉默是不可原谅的。“

Full List of Toxic Chemicals Released From Ohio Train Derailment --- 俄亥俄州火车出轨事件释放有毒化学物质完整清单
https://www.newsweek.com/ohio-train-derailment-toxic-chemicals-list-epa-1780805

####  UnhappyTails  
##### 318#       发表于 2023-2-14 02:10

 本帖最后由 UnhappyTails 于 2023-2-14 05:18 编辑 

美国在大众媒体时代进行的主流媒体机器改造，其核心不在于建立起亲民或广为传播的媒体机器，那些信息主流媒体是无法和茧房中的意见领袖竞争的，如果经常关注美国主流媒体，你会发现美国媒体的主要武器恰恰是似乎与大众媒体时代背道而驰的权威性

打个比方，如果今天有人跟你说，日本岛沉没了快庆祝，你是第一时间弹冠相庆开始二次传播，还是先去社交媒体上看看权威媒体确认是不是真的发生了这样的事情呢？如果主流媒体报道了这个事情，那无论主流媒体对这件事采取什么样的态度，大概率你还是会相信日本沉没了，而且沉的好。可如果没有主流媒体报道这件事，那么你别说庆祝了，大概率是觉得日本沉没这个事实也只是群里的群友异想天开罢了。

现代社会的主流媒体，很多时候需要的不是观点的影响力或者代表性，而恰恰是事实上的权威性。一旦这种权威性被构建起来，那么即便你的观点无法代表任何人，你依然能在人的价值判断上起到非常大的作用。而且无论是无中生有进行完全的抹黑虚假的报道还是把一件惊天动地的大事以极低的成本消弭，只要有如此权威性或者说“真实性”的媒体足够抛弃底线，就可以在舆论场中产生极强的，且不易被人察觉的引导能力，而美国主流媒体权威，中立，甚至有些过于古板保守的面具下，恰恰是超乎想象的无耻和恶劣，正是这种伪装和内核的彻底背道而驰才让这些主流媒体在互联网媒体时代依旧能够轻易占据一席之地。

当然了，将这些媒体利益集团人格化的意义也不大，说是有意地捂盖子，其实无非就是和政府进行了内部交易罢了。更不用说怕此类新闻本身就缺乏炒作空间，欧美极度缺位的公职人员问责机制也明确了这样的报道不可能带来老百姓希望的正义（老百姓也早就不在乎那些争议了），这使得这类报道没有什么利润率可言，这些媒体自然也没动力去说真话。

回到这次俄亥俄州的事情，我们来看看各大媒体的反应。事故发生后，大媒体都是简单报道了此次事件的爆炸部分，而对车内具体的有害物质语焉不详或者干脆闭口不提，至于提到聚乙烯和二噁英的更是寥寥

很多人将这件事归咎于俄亥俄州政府的能力低下，但其实有毒气体这件事情大部分媒体当天或是第二天就知道了（几乎所有的报道原文里都提到了hazardous material，但对详细种类，危害等等闭口不谈），但将其放入标题的媒体却寥寥无几，这和大家十分熟悉的，惯于做标题党的西方媒体形象显然是极为不符合的

[https://www.cnn.com/2023/02/05/u ... e-sunday/index.html](https://www.cnn.com/2023/02/05/us/east-palestine-ohio-train-derailment-fire-sunday/index.html) cnn，标题中只提到了大火和疏散

[https://www.nytimes.com/2023/02/ ... palestine-ohio.html](https://www.nytimes.com/2023/02/04/us/train-derailment-fire-palestine-ohio.html) 扭腰时报，标题中同样只提到了大火和疏散

[https://www.bbc.com/news/av/world-us-canada-64525073](https://www.bbc.com/news/av/world-us-canada-64525073) 张宏圣，特别短的报道，同样只提到了大火，都没提疏散

[https://news.yahoo.com/flames-rage-huge-fire-train-074004722.html](https://news.yahoo.com/flames-rage-huge-fire-train-074004722.html) 雅虎，只提到了大火，疏散都没有提到

[https://www.wsj.com/articles/ohi ... al-town-11675630255](https://www.wsj.com/articles/ohio-train-derailment-fire-rattle-rural-town-11675630255) 华尔街时报，同样只提到了大火

而且虽然这几篇文章中都或多或少提到了车上可能有危险物质，但是在标题中却隐隐将俄亥俄州的疏散归结为爆炸而非有毒物质

[https://www.theguardian.com/us-n ... -evacuation-warning](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2023/feb/06/ohio-train-derailment-evacuation-warning) 第一篇在标题中提到有毒有害物质的是<strong>英国卫报</strong>，此时已经是2.6，距离爆炸发生已经过去足足两天

<strong>“俄亥俄州发生火车越轨事故，州长疏散民众”</strong>和<strong>“俄亥俄州发生火车越轨事故，州长承认有害化学物质可能已经泄露扩散”</strong>这两个标题哪一个更有流量更能吸睛，相信即便不是新闻背景的谭友也一目了然，无论是追求阅读量的媒体还是追求正义和社会贡献的媒体，怎么会抛弃后者采用前者呢？

而大多数网民本身就已经对这些事件提不起兴趣，加上标题中刻意往“普通的生产安全事故，不会对产生任何深远影响”进行引导，导致根本没有人对这件事形成任何的重视，自然也缺乏茧房当中的讨论度，并且在国际社会也引不起任何波澜了

在这整件事情当中，仅仅靠这种细微的偏差报道和重点转移，辅以对其他有炒作价值的新闻进行反复地炒作报道和社交媒体煽动对立，美国媒体轻而易举的将需要引起重视的事情捂住，将不需要引起重视的事情捧起。全美国乃至全世界的网民乃至老百姓也就跟着这些媒体的指挥棒来回摆动。直到俄亥俄州一名记者遭到逮捕，形成了一个极有炒作空间的触发点（其实也就是阴谋论所需要的“边角料”，讽刺吧，美国的大新闻需要阴谋论者推动才会曝光）以后，网民们才大梦初醒开始跟进报道渲染，于是这起生态灾难才慢慢暴露在大众面前。更不用说，在这整起事件期间，州政府官方，美国那些所谓的既中立又善良的化学科学家和工程师，以及一向冲在前面的时刻监视民主政治运作的大众媒体kol们完全失位

这就是美国媒体的可怕之处，他的强大已经完全不体现在明目张胆的封堵，引导和歪曲了，而是通过这种伪装的权威性和高超的话术以及超乎想象的毫无底线，将一件应该被讨论的事彻底掩埋，至于媒体人的责任和这样的报道导致的灾难，毁掉的家庭，和造成的牺牲，对于这些新一代美国主流媒体人来说，这根本就不是一件值得考虑的事情

而中下层教育水平越来越低下的美国普罗大众别说反抗，就连理解这种高明舆论战的知识基础都没有，在灭顶之灾面前表现得就像一个个孩子，民众们热衷放在嘴上的所谓的自由意志再这样荒诞的背景下显得格外地可笑

冷战后传播学的研究开辟了选举政治这个新的发挥舞台和互联网这个新阵地，对媒体传播的引导和操控已经是以前的成果了，最新的应该是剑桥数据和棱镜系统这种的

####  半分宅  
##### 337#       发表于 2023-2-14 07:03

美国国家环境保护局的[update](https://response.epa.gov/sites/15933/files/Norfolk%20Southern%20East%20Palestine%20Train%20Derailment%20General%20Notice%20Letter%202.10.2023.pdf)：

5车氯乙烯被排入壕沟烧掉，列车上运载的其他化工产品包括乙二醇单丁醚(Ethylene Glycol Monobutyl Ether），丙烯酸异辛酯（ethylhexyl acrylate），异丁烯（Isobutylene），丙烯酸丁酯（Butyl acrylate）

Below is a brief description of the actions and observations taken by EPA at the Site to date:
Conducted air monitoring around the scene of the incident, the surrounding community, and residential air monitoring as part of the re-occupancy plan;
Conducted air and water sampling;
Made the following observations:

a. Materials released during the incident were observed and detected in samples from Sulphur Run, Leslie Run, Bull Creek, North Fork Little Beaver Creek, Little Beaver Creek, and the Ohio River.

b. Materials related to the incident were observed entering storm drains.

c. Multiple rail cars and tankers were observed derailed, breached, and/or on fire,

that included but not limited to the following materials:

Vinyl chloride
Ethylene glycol monobutyl ether
Ethylhexyl acrylate
Isobutylene
Butyl acrylate.

d. Five rail car tankers of vinyl chloride were intentionally breached; the vinyl

chloride was diverted to an excavated trench and then burned off.

e. Areas of contaminated soil and free liquids were observed and potentially covered

and/or filled during reconstruction of the rail line including portions of the trench /burn pit that was used for the open burn off of vinyl chloride.

美国自21年败登上台后，110多个农场食品厂家禽场化肥厂食品配送中心遭遇不明火灾，食品供应链受到严重影响，造成食品短缺价格飙升。最近竟然发生装满有毒化学药品的火车脱轨事故，10天内已经发生3起！

🚃 2月3号，100多节化学药品的火车在Ohio East Palestein与卡车相撞脱轨，造成大火，严重污染了附近的河水，农田和空气；这起事故很可能是美国历史上最重大的环境生态灾难之一。

🚃  2月13号下午，南卡罗来纳州伊诺雷市(Enoree)的火车脱轨，目前没有进一步信息发布。

🚃  2月13号下午，德州休斯顿附近火车脱轨。官员报道火车承载有毒物质，会对脱轨地点附近空气造成污染。 

10天之内发生3起火车脱轨事件，这是巧合吗？败登ZF到现在为止吭都不吭一声。 [http://t.cn/A6Cz4VLE](http://t.cn/A6Cz4VLE)

####  HZLJ  
##### 392#       发表于 2023-2-14 11:15

 本帖最后由 HZLJ 于 2023-2-14 11:17 编辑 
<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59734565&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">Mr.Cheung 发表于 2023-2-13 23:54</a>

其实还真没有这么简单</blockquote>
[https://www.supplychaindive.com/news/norfolk-southern-psr-transition/548231/](https://www.supplychaindive.com/news/norfolk-southern-psr-transition/548231/)
 <blockquote>Norfolk Southern 周一在亚特兰大铁路新总部举行的投资者会议上制定了实施精确预定铁路 (PSR) 的计划。该计划包括集中运营、裁员、运行更少、更重、更快的列车以及优化网络以提高效率。 
为了到 2021 年实现 60% 的运营率（目前为 65.4%），铁路将在 2019 年裁员 500 人，到 2021 年裁员 3,000 人。 

其中一些变化已经开始，特别是列车速度和停留时间的改进，这是铁路制定如此紧迫的过渡时间表的部分原因，到 2021 年实现 PSR 的全面实施。 </blockquote><blockquote>在演示中，Norfolk Southern 的高管们谈到了 PSR 的所有最大亮点：更快和更重的火车、火车和员工的生产力、更高的火车速度和减少的停留时间。铁路正在尝试实施这些原则，同时改善客户服务，这在过去的 PSR 转型中一直是一个症结所在。 

Norfolk Southern 去年推出了一个数字客户门户网站，以帮助管理货运和提高知名度。它是围绕做它所说的它要做的事情“采用口头禅”——即使这意味着做的更少。首席执行官吉姆斯奎尔斯表示，铁路将改变其服务并以不同的方式优先考虑负载，以“明确我们能做什么和不能做什么”，这将导致一些客户流失。

“随着我们通过 PSR，服务将会发生变化。考虑到大多数客户需求的网络不会对每个客户都是理想的，”Squires 说。 

**解释说，成功将通过三个指标来判断： 

服务交付指数 (SDI)，这是一种基于铁路是否履行其对客户做出的承诺的指标——首席运营官 Mike Wheeler 暗示，这是一种比常见的 PSR 标准旅行计划合规性 (TPI) 更以客户为中心的衡量标准.

火车和员工的生产率是通过每位在职机组人员移动的交通量来衡量的。

在线车辆以每列火车的吨位计量。

最终所有的指标将是运营比率 (OR)——一个反映铁路整体效率的单一数字。Norfolk Southern 的目标是到 2021 年达到 60%，希望与其他采用 PSR 的铁路保持一致，去年所有这些铁路的 OR 都低于 62%。</blockquote>
[https://higherlogicdownload.s3.a ... 2019_v1_0_Cheng.pdf](https://higherlogicdownload.s3.amazonaws.com/INFORMS/e52cec4c-eedb-4c3b-a379-8408d89f8fc9/UploadedImages/2019_Seattle/INFORMS_PSR_2019_v1_0_Cheng.pdf)

Norfolk Southern 就是本次火车脱轨事故的当事公司

 <blockquote>RWU 认为，过时的监管和企业不当行为导致了可能对世代造成破坏的事件，其罪魁祸首是精确调度铁路 (PSR)。这种做法被一些工人称为“积极的股东反应”，它通过单个车厢而不是整列火车来管理货运移动——确保火车车厢始终在移动。实际上，这导致裁员、合并调度中心并降低了火车的安全性，因为更少的工人没有更多时间检查更多的火车车厢。

根据其分析，RWU 表示，“事故的直接原因似乎是其中一节车厢的车轴发生了 19 世纪风格的机械故障——轴承过热——导致脱轨，然后折断车厢翻滚。”

此外，火车的整体重量似乎不平衡；在 PSR 之前，核心小组说，火车将在头部建造较重的车厢，而较轻的车厢在后方。这样的做法可以防止发生在俄亥俄州的事情：较重的汽车在他们面前猛撞较轻的汽车，导致上周发生的确切的折叠。据称，这列火车的 40% 的重量都集中在火车后部的三分之一处。

幸运的是，尽管发生了这些故障，列车上的三名乘务员还是能够迅速齐心协力，将损失降到最低。由于铁路公司厚颜无耻地提议只裁减一名成员，谢天谢地，这里的情况并非如此。

RWU 表示：“NS 和其他 1 级铁路的短期利润需求，即所谓的‘运营比率崇拜’，已将削减成本、员工、程序和资源列为首要任务。” Norfolk Southern 最近公布了创纪录的第四季度和年度收入；就在去年，该公司宣布了100 亿美元的股票回购。与此同时，它的员工甚至连带薪病假都得不到保证。

这里的工人发出警告之前，人们一直在开展争取更好的工作条件和更安全的铁路成果的运动。在政府于 12 月向工人强加一份不包括急需的带薪病假的合同后，工人们继续为此类福利以及至少两人制船员的保证和 PSR 的取消而集会。

尽管如此，在国情咨文中，拜登总统并没有提及铁路工人的困境，甚至也没有讨论灾难性的铁路脱轨事件。然而，工人们的努力并没有完全被忽视；参议员伯尼桑德斯和迈克布劳恩将于周四举行新闻发布会，要求铁路工人休带薪病假。

“32N 号列车的残骸已经酝酿多年。RWU 说：“等待我们的还有哪些类似的火车残骸，还有待观察。” “但考虑到一级铁路承运人的作案手法，我们无疑可以预见未来会发生这种性质的灾难。”</blockquote>
[https://newrepublic.com/post/170 ... n-derailment-happen](https://newrepublic.com/post/170455/rail-workers-tried-warn-us-ohio-train-derailment-happen)

####  samuel.j  
##### 398#       发表于 2023-2-14 11:22

<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59734565&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">Mr.Cheung 发表于 2023-2-13 23:54</a>

其实还真没有这么简单</blockquote>
简单地说，PSR约等于将原有相对编组站-支线模式的传统铁路货运带来革新的图定班列模式进一步迅速化，完全像当代公路货运那样做到随有货随开车，间接需要足够的司乘与工务人员维持整个系统的运作。

但是相对于西方国家卡车与网约车行业可以轻松“开发”到外劳人矿甚至非法移民资源的“优势”，需要长时间技术培训积累的美国铁路司机与随车工程师并没有轻松到直接发绿卡画个大饼就能糊弄到一堆第三世界劳动者轻松投靠，结果资本家们只能进一步为节约利润压迫既有铁路职工，整个劳动环境回到1877年。如果这只是货运系统剥削压迫的例子，现在可以想到客运系统的一个范例：以极高列车准点率，与全日本私铁最大列车编组12节快特列车而闻名的京滨急行在疫情前后被揭出为维持高密度运行图，司乘近乎全日处于极高的工作压力下，以至于问题丛生。

作为交通研究者，我不觉得衰落已久美国铁路客运完全没有可取之处，起码新建设的几个客运项目与改造工程的设计理念与美国/加拿大的重载货运相同，非常值得敝国同行们在将来的新基建投资与改造中加以借鉴与本土化改造

*****

####  bubeby  
##### 399#       发表于 2023-2-14 11:23

Basically, above 700 or so, and it's dioxon free.

Below 400, you don't get dioxins, you just get oddly chlorinated chemical and bad chemical shit. Not Great, Not terrible. Might get cancer.

Between 400 - 700 and the richer (sootier) you burn, the worse the dioxin.

400～700度，烟越多，二恶英越多

####  vamr  
##### 429#       发表于 2023-2-14 12:26

<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59739160&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">勿徊哉 发表于 2023-2-14 12:01</a>

有机物在环境中应该过几个礼拜就没有毒性了吧？

不像放射物存在好几十年 ...</blockquote>
装聋作哑的那个人懒得理他

个人看法就是原来泄露的氯乙烯本身量大、剧毒，一级致癌物不假，但是原地渗透和蒸发毁灭的还是美国本土一州的土壤、水源，氯乙烯不稳定容易被自然光解，那么较短的时间内空气中的是有可能自然降解处理掉的，这样的土地生产出来的农作物喂牲畜，牲畜再喂人，环环降解损耗。有毒、致癌，但是有盼头。

燃烧产物的二噁英，本身剧毒、是氰化物的上百倍，毒性致癌性超过氯乙烯，燃烧过程中黑烟直升而上飞速扩散，因为不懂气象学不知道上没上升到平流程——平流程那就全球扩散。然后二噁英很难自然降解，半衰期长，百科上称之为“世纪之毒”污染的土地出产物吸收多少二噁英，做成食物和饲料那么就原汁原味汇总到食用者体内富集，顿顿吃这样的污染物的人体内浓度可能比地里刨食的鸡鸡鸭鸭还高。什么时候环境能自我净化完成，某感觉有生之年是看不到了。

####  Diong  
##### 457#       发表于 2023-2-14 14:11

<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59741037&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">阿拉纳克 发表于 2023-2-14 14:06</a>
这个大概是这次燃烧会产生二恶英的原因？</blockquote>
在知乎上翻了半天看到的一个引用，主要是含氯环境下有机物的不完全燃烧。

二噁英前驱物可以是氯苯、氯酚等二噁英类片段物质；也可能是脂肪族化合物、芳香族化合物、氯代烃等化合物，在有活性氯的氛围中，在燃烧后区域的高温段《大于400℃，最有效的范围是 750℃)通过环化及氯化等过程形成。二噁英前驱物大都由燃料的不完全燃烧产生。反应所需的活性氯如活性氯原子和氯气，主要由HCI氧化生成

https://d.wanfangdata.com.cn/periodical/ChlQZ**b2RpY2FsQ0**mV3UzIwMjMwMTEyEg94enF5a2oyMDA4MjYxNzMaCDRyOTV4cXh4

 <blockquote>我知道有些人要拿张家口那次氯乙烯泄露说事。

有奇葩人士，说张家口那次泄露氯乙烯2046立方米，换算成加仑，就是54万加仑，美国俄亥俄这次才10万加仑。

他们故意混淆了，或者隐去了一个事实，就是张家口那次泄露的是气体，而俄亥俄这次泄露的是液体。

氯乙烯的气体密度是2.77公斤每立方米，液体密度是903公斤每立方米。

2046立方米氯乙烯气体换算成质量，是5.6吨。

10万加仑氯乙烯液体换算成质量，是378吨。

张家口泄露的氯乙烯连美国的零头都不到。

不知这些人的居心何在？</blockquote>

目前美国EPA事件相关问题回复，每天更新一次。

EPA最新说法是：Re-Entry air screenings are underway. Community air monitoring will continue operating 24 hours a day. As of yesterday evening, 291 homes have been screened. To date, no detections of vinyl chloride or hydrogen chloride were identified for the completed screened homes. There are 181 homes that remain to be screened.

U.S. EPA has deployed two more Summa air sampling canisters for continuous sampling. Local schools and the library were screened yesterday.

US EPA’s network of air monitoring stations throughout the East Palestine area did not detect anything above the action level.

是压缩的液化气体，沸点-13度，泄漏了就一直在挥发，所谓倒出来其实是把液化的气体倒出来，室温下一直在爆沸蒸发可燃气体，你拿管子抽因为管内压强肯定比大气压低不可能抽出任何液体，一旦烧起来更加加剧挥发就不可能灭了。

####  LeonsCat  
##### 608#       发表于 2023-2-15 11:21

<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59753631&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">snoopys 发表于 2023-2-15 11:08</a>

还有一点

我们确实不能用中国式思维理解外国</blockquote>
如果所有槽罐整体完整无损坏，那最好的方法大概是拉走处理。

但是只要有一个已经开始泄漏，考虑到那鬼地方短时间内十有八九拉不出能在危化泄漏现场转移未损坏的槽罐的抢险人员，都烧了怕真是多害相权取其轻。。。

氯乙烯这玩意室温下是气体，上百吨一旦扩散会产生严重的光化学污染，那个是催化性质一传十十传百，一发不可收拾。相反烧了的话，考虑到好歹是气气燃烧，再不完全不会比露天烧上几百上千吨废旧PVC还要燃烧不完全、污染大……就算污染物要么碳颗粒要么盐酸，再不行那点二噁英也算上，都属于下场雨就能比较好沉降的，也就霍霍当地，氯乙烯气体本身除了光化学分解外还挺惰性的，天知道飘到那个大城市那才叫玩球。

<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59754384&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">嘟帝 发表于 2023-2-15 12:04</a>

你不废话，氟化氢怎么烧</blockquote><blockquote>12月18日16时许，一辆载有20多吨粗苯的危险化学品槽罐车行至陕西临兴高速泾阳县三渠段时，由于法兰破裂造成粗苯泄漏。司机拨打报警电话请求救援。

粗苯属于危化品，具有可燃、致癌毒性、易引起燃烧爆炸等危险特性。接到报警后，陕西省应急管理厅开展线上救援“云指挥”，组织市县两级政府相关部门成立应急处置机构，封锁事故路段，第一时间前往处置、安全救援。咸阳市应急管理局启动应急预案联动程序，要求境内的大型化工企业延长石油兴化公司进行应急救援专业协助。该公司当日值班的安环质监部副部长杨尔兴，根据命令迅速带领有关人员携带正压式空气呼吸器、过滤式面罩和重型防化服，向现场火速驰援。

18时40分，兴化公司应急救援人员赶到现场，指挥机构授权杨尔兴担任现场指挥，制定了应急处置方案，组织调度消防、交通、专业倒罐、医疗救护等力量，全面开展现场事故应急处置。

现场情况复杂严峻，空气中弥漫着刺鼻的气味，随时存在着火、爆炸和中毒等危险因素。随着夜幕降临，气温下降到-7℃左右，在指导所有处置人员佩戴好防护用具后，救援队伍进入现场对险情进行了详细勘察和研判，按照处置方案，消防队一边使用泡沫覆盖，限制有害气体挥发，技术人员一边利用专业设备进行倒罐操作，公安、交通负责现场警戒，医疗人员则随时待命应对人员突发状况。

19时58分，两辆车完成了罐口对接开始倒罐作业，所有人员撤离至安全地带。21时50分左右，涉事车辆中剩余的苯全部转移至处置车辆中。22时20分，消防队对现场环境完成了最后洗消，现场处置基本完成，泄漏物由专业危险化学品处置单位妥善处理，相关人员陆续撤离，高速公路有序恢复通行。事故未造成环境危害。（杨锡勇 魏飞）</blockquote>
怎么回事呢，这不还是美国人菜？

　　据杭州市消防支队有关人员介绍，实际情况是因为14日晚间的一场车祸，救援人员至今仍在对事故涉及的危化品进行倒罐。为以防万一，组织了附近人员适当疏散。

　　14日22时36分左右，杭州绕城高速公路三墩往留下方向位于留下收费站不到76公路处，一辆装有120桶20吨的树脂大挂车撞上了一辆载有27吨氯乙烯的槽罐车，导致大挂车与槽罐车同时撞破护栏翻倒路基下6－7米的沟中。

　　消防人员介绍说，氯乙烯是一种有毒气体，轻度中毒时，会出现眩晕、胸闷、嗜睡等症状，严重中毒可发生昏迷、抽搐、甚至死亡；树脂也是易燃有毒物质，两者一旦发生泄漏，后果不堪设想。

　　为了尽快飞把“炸弹”移走，高速交警、消防、环保相关部门积极商讨对策。经了解槽罐车的罐壁太薄，在起吊中槽罐车罐壁可能会承受不住整个车身重量而导致罐体破裂。15日，高速交警等部门决定对侧翻的槽罐车进行倒罐。

　　截至记者16日上午发稿时，倒罐工作仍在进行中。</blockquote>

####  苏西踩到我了  
##### 662#       发表于 2023-2-15 13:56

宠物圈子开始讨论这事的影响，渴望这些美国猫粮都是五大湖周边的，肯定不能买了，养猫的在找替代品。那么，优质国产猫粮销量肯定会暴增，国内宠物赛道投资也会更多。

我意识到，这件事的影响肯定会比我们想象得更大。

美国能维持全球霸主的基础之一，是能用廉价的农产品赎买底层，保证稳定。如果底层发现本土的农产品不能吃了，必然引起混乱。混乱到一定程度就是动乱，所以为了维稳，美国必然会加大农产品的进口，买不到就抢。
世界主要粮食产区就那么几个，而且前几年因为各种原因，全球粮食已经减产了，不少国家禁止粮食出口。
那么……俄乌很可能因此停战？
政治都如此，更别说资本市场了，必然一片腥风血雨。
（后续的癌症反而是小事，真得癌症了得多少年以后，整活能力也会变差，政府提供几桶止痛药问题就解决了。美国政府怕就怕这些害怕自己得癌症的健康人。）

事故发生地的本地，肯定不能住人了，当地人搬迁到别的城市，会引发各种矛盾，房子、工作岗位、教育，还有更重要的选票，加上这些人大都是武德充沛的红脖子，发生什么事都不过分。

这事真是超级无敌的黑天鹅，会动摇美国国本。

####  myarms  
##### 690#       发表于 2023-2-15 15:16

我觉得这不是单纯烧不烧的问题，楼里争论的，是有没有烧的替代方案，我决定这是其中的一个方面，有没有对烧之外的方案做过评估，那些替代方案之所以不采用，是基于什么原因？

另外是烧这个处置方案的这个决定，是谁下的命令，是政府、环境部门、还是这家铁路公司？这个处置方案是为了快速解决案发现场化学物质泄漏，还是一个有考虑到后续环境影响，以及受灾范围整体居民安置的一个完整计划？

很深层次或者很专业的东西我不懂，但从中文网络能看得的消息看来，烧这个决定，和后续的环境影响预判，以及受灾居民的安置，包括受灾范围的判断，是存在一定程度上的误判和延误的，这些都是让我这些不懂专业知识的人，感到烧这个处置，给人感觉不严谨或者存在不恰当处理的原因


*****

####  与太郎  
##### 729#       发表于 2023-2-15 17:01

<blockquote>2023 年 2 月 14 日更新  

今天下午早些时候，美国环保署地区署长黛布拉·肖尔就俄亥俄州东巴勒斯坦的应急响应发表了声明。该声明可在此处获取： https: //www.epa.gov/newsreleases/statement-regional-administrator-debra-shore-east-palestine-train-derailment  

2月13日晚，美国环保署停止对光气和氯化氢社区空气监测进行空气监测。2月8日大火被扑灭后，氯乙烯火灾产生光气和氯化氢的威胁不复存在。美国环保署将继续对其他受关注的化学物质进行 24 小时社区空气监测。  

截至 2 月 13 日结束时，美国环保署已对 396 户家庭的室内空气进行了筛查，剩余 100 户，今天计划对 65 户家庭进行检测。 

2023 年 2 月 13 日更新 

重新进入空气筛选正在进行中。社区空气监测将继续全天 24 小时运行。截至昨天晚上，已经对 291 所房屋进行了筛查。迄今为止，已完成筛查的房屋未检测到氯乙烯或氯化氢。还有 181 所房屋有待筛选。

US EPA 又部署了两个 Summa 空气采样罐进行连续采样。昨天对当地学校和图书馆进行了筛查。

美国环保署遍布东巴勒斯坦地区的空气监测站网络未检测到任何高于行动水平的物质。 </blockquote>

####  阿卡林的存在感  
##### 748#       发表于 2023-2-15 18:26

既然事实大致可以确定了，就用高中水平知识来解说一下毒性问题，
耍流氓地谈一下毒性强弱，那大致就是，某些氯乙烯不完全燃烧产物&gt;常见剧毒物质&gt;氯乙烯&gt;苯=苯不完全燃烧&gt;大众所说剧毒物&gt;事故中列出的其他化学品&gt;氯乙烯完全燃烧
氯乙烯跟苯的接触限值相同，但氯乙烯致死量更低一些。不是要跟美帝人民共情的就不必拿氯乙烯和苯以外那些东西说事了，相较之下那些都是小问题而已。

如果要不耍流氓地讨论，那么设想一定量污染物在一平方公里五米高度内空气中均匀分布，按照标准，氯乙烯要求低于50公斤，二噁英是2.5克。哪种危害大就等价于50公斤氯乙烯产生的二噁英有没有2.5克，说实话这个我不知道所以没办法给出回答。
按报道，氯乙烯总量应该不到200吨，那么污染范围理论值上限就是4000平方公里。

####  gorilla994  
##### 860#       发表于 2023-2-18 04:08

1950年9月20日到27日，美国海军在旧金山海岸，释放了一批粘质沙雷氏菌气溶胶，测试生物武器对于城市攻击的效果，通过监测站的数据，美军得到了扩散的数据。 但是在10月的时候，旧金山的肺炎发病率提高，有少数人出现了严重的罕见感染。而对于这次行动，美军之前并没有什么警告或者是通知。解密之后美国人民才得知这次事件，而因为罕见感染死亡的一个病人的家属起诉美国军方，要求赔偿，但是赔偿要求被拒绝了。 有医学家研究觉得，这个事长期改变了旧金山土壤和湾区的微生物结构，永久性提高了旧金山肺炎发病率。 还有别的什么，比如往纽约地铁扔装满了“无害”病原体的灯泡，往华盛顿机场的车站散布病原体什么的。 50-70年代这方面的实验，美国官方承认了的大概有239次。 不承认的成为都市传说的有上千次。 比如美国一个典型的阴谋论观点，认为北美大陆的莱姆病流行，是美国当年昆虫生物武器玩脱了。

####  vamr  
##### 906#       发表于 2023-2-20 15:33

 本帖最后由 vamr 于 2023-2-20 15:36 编辑 

EPA 对脱轨事件环境监测的动态更新：[https://response.epa.gov/site/site_profile.aspx?site_id=15933](https://response.epa.gov/site/site_profile.aspx?site_id=15933)

Updates

Feb. 19, 2023

Air Monitoring &amp; Indoor Air Screening: U.S. EPA continues real-time air monitoring and collecting air samples throughout the community. Air monitoring and sampling will continue until removal of heavily contaminated soil in the derailment area is complete and odors subside in the community.

U.S. EPA also continues to assist indoor air screenings in homes. To date, 533 homes have been screened with no exceedances for residential air quality standards. There are 15 homes scheduled for indoor air screening today.

Municipal Water: The Village of East Palestine’s municipal well water sample results show no water quality concerns. The Columbiana County Health District continues to sample private water wells. To date, 52 wells have been sampled, 49 in Ohio, and 3 in Pennsylvania.

Norfolk Southern is supplying bottled water at their Family Assistance Center. For more information about the center, including location and operating hours please, visit Norfolk Southern’s website.

Derailment Site Soil: U.S. EPA continues to support Ohio EPA in the state’s ongoing and future cleanup activities for the incident, including water quality efforts.

Norfolk Southern continued scrapping and removing rail cars at the derailment location, excavating contaminated areas, removing contaminated liquids from affected storm drains, and staging recovered waste for transportation to an approved disposal facility. Water continues to be diverted from the upstream wetland area to Sulphur Run.

机翻：
<strong>空气监测和室内空气筛查： </strong>美国环保署继续对整个社区进行实时空气监测和空气样本采集。空气监测和采样将继续进行，直到完成脱轨区域严重污染的土壤清除工作并且社区中的气味消退。美国环保署还继续协助家庭进行室内空气筛查。迄今为止，已对 533 户家庭进行了筛查，未发现空气质量超标。今天计划对 15 个家庭进行室内空气筛查。<strong>市政供水： </strong>东巴勒斯坦村的市政井水样本结果显示没有水质问题。哥伦比亚县卫生区继续对私人水井进行采样。迄今为止，已对 52 口井进行了采样，其中 49 口在俄亥俄州，3 口在宾夕法尼亚州。Norfolk Southern 正在其家庭援助中心供应瓶装水。有关该中心的更多信息，包括位置和营业时间，请访问 [Norfolk Southern 的网站](https://gcc02.safelinks.protection.outlook.com/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fnscorp.mediaroom.com%2Fassistance-center&amp;data=05%7C01%7CMichalos.Maria%40epa.gov%7C8670f0ac697b4359d66c08db12afcb51%7C88b378b367484867acf976aacbeca6a7%7C0%7C0%7C638124318463569900%7CUnknown%7CTWFpbGZsb3d8eyJWIjoiMC4wLjAwMDAiLCJQIjoiV2luMzIiLCJBTiI6Ik1haWwiLCJXVCI6Mn0%3D%7C3000%7C%7C%7C&amp;sdata=pkNLEmzgLsfNb8qjLSnz%2F7jP7tJk5rAaaLSt0VFfZEk%3D&amp;reserved=0)。<strong>出轨现场土壤：</strong> 美国环保局继续支持俄亥俄州环保局在该州正在进行和未来的事件清理活动，包括水质工作。Norfolk Southern 继续报废和拆除出轨地点的轨道车，挖掘受污染的区域，从受影响的雨水渠中清除受污染的液体，并将回收的废物转移到经批准的处置设施。水继续从上游湿地区域转移到 Sulphur Run。
居民区的空气和水好像暂时还好，土壤标本尚未回报。

####  HZLJ  
##### 920#       发表于 2023-2-21 10:53

 本帖最后由 HZLJ 于 2023-2-21 10:55 编辑 
<blockquote>财联社上海2月21日讯（编辑 黄君芝）美国俄亥俄州火车脱轨事件才过去没多久，当地又发生一起重大事故。

据报道，该州贝德福德市的一家金属制造厂周一（20日）又发生爆炸。有官员和目击者称，熔化的金属和碎片散落在附近的建筑物上，造成至少14人受伤，其中大多数人被烧伤。

据悉，I. Schumann &amp; Co.金属工厂发生爆炸后，浓烟四起，直冲云霄上千米高空。有附近居民称，30公里外都能看见巨大蘑菇云。俄亥俄州东北部各地的消防部门均已出动。

image

奥克伍德消防队（Oakwood Fire Department）队长Brian DiRocco在现场对媒体说，有13人被送往医院，其中许多人有烧伤，还有一人正在现场接受治疗。

事故中，至少一人伤势严重，还有一人从废墟中被救出。DiRocco还说，所幸的是，所有受伤的人都为现场人员，坠落的碎片未伤及附近企业的员工。

“这些人大多是受了伤。”他补充说，“我相信在这里工作的很多人都感到震惊。”

事实上，这已是俄亥俄州本月发生的第二场事故了。本月早些时候，一列满载有毒化学物质的火车脱轨，随后当地部门的处理方式又导致了大量的有毒气体排放到空气中，迫使数千人撤离。

I.Schumann &amp; Co.是一家金属制造厂，生产铜、黄铜和青铜制品，记者无法立即联系到该公司的代表置评。据其网站介绍，该公司自1917年开始运营。DiRocco说他以前检查过该工厂，并认为它是一个安全的地方，“不过，你在处理熔化的金属，所以总是有内在的危险。”

附近公司Rose Colored Gaming的老板Matthew Wiggins表示，他听到了一声巨大的爆炸声，“在一两秒钟内，听起来就像大量的碎片击中了屋顶。”

“东西从墙上掉下来，从架子上掉下来。我们走到前面，院子里有冒烟的岩石和熔化的金属。成吨成吨的烟。大火从街对面的大楼里滚滚而出。”他说。

另一名目击者Joe Sarconi说，他当时正在街对面的车里吃午饭，突然听到至少两声爆炸声，包围房子的砖墙被炸飞。</blockquote>
[https://www.cls.cn/detail/1272671](https://www.cls.cn/detail/1272671)

####  与太郎  
##### 921#       发表于 2023-2-21 10:58

[有没有化工大佬可以科普一下，俄亥俄氯乙烯泄露及后续点燃处理事件的危害程度到底如何？ - Dr.张狒狒的回答 - 知乎](https://www.zhihu.com/question/583964280/answer/2895774151)
 <blockquote>按这份报告的数据来估测，20~380吨氯乙烯在空气中灼烧，会产生2~38吨灰烬，会产生140~2660克二噁英。这些二噁英主要集中在灰烬之中，灰烬落下之前，土壤中的二噁英含量不会很高，TCDD熔点305℃，常温下是固体，空气中自然是检测不出来，VOC自然也没有意义。TCDD在水中的溶解度是 0.2μg/L，而如果只检测土壤，而剥落表层灰烬，土壤中未检出二噁英几乎是必然，但二噁英在土壤中降解的半衰期为12年。</blockquote>

知乎上有这么个回答<img src="https://static.saraba1st.com/image/smiley/face2017/009.gif" referrerpolicy="no-referrer">这和之前另一个谭友的说法确实不太一样

<blockquote><a href="httphttps://bbs.saraba1st.com/2b/forum.php?mod=redirect&amp;goto=findpost&amp;pid=59830846&amp;ptid=2119338" target="_blank">Karajan 发表于 2023-2-21 09:29</a>

EPA最早的报告不是说没有问题么？我记得vinyl chloride好像含量不到1ppm，怎么就有污染土壤了？有相关检 ...</blockquote>
epa官方链接给你了，下面有目前公布的档案，只看文件名基本都是air air air air。土壤的还没公布。

土壤污染一是脱轨地方直接撒了一地的小范围，这个不用化验肯定有污染，也没人在乎。需要在乎的肯定是广泛的人口居住区与农产品种植生产区域在焚烧物随降水下降回底面后的污染情况，这个还没公布。必然是个长期结果。不是一锤子买卖。今天烧上天明天就化验土壤的肯定不是准确结果，烧的灰还在天上飘着呢。要长期观察
